252 if (t && t.insertAdjacentElement) {

253 t.insertAdjacentElement('afterend', s);

254 } else {

255 d.head.appendChild(s);

256 }

257 ++this.index;

258 },

259

260 createScript: function (script, beforeLoad) {

261 var s = d.createElement('script');

262 s.id = 'js-position' + (this.index + 1);

263 s.setAttribute('data-test', script.test);

264 if (beforeLoad) {

265 s.defer = 'defer';

266 s.onload = function () {

267 if (script.noinit) {

268 loader.register(true);

269 }

270 if (d.readyState === 'interactive' || d.readyState === 'complete') {

271 loader.ready();

272 }

273 };

274 } else {

275 s.async = 'async';

276 }

277 s.src = script.src;

278 return s;

279 },

280

281 init: function () {

282 this.scripts.forEach(function (s) {

283 loader.insert(loader.createScript(s, true));

284 });

285

286 d.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {

287 loader.ready();

288

289 var conditionalScripts = [

290 {match: 'div[data-pan-container]', src: '/static/js/pan-zoom-es6-bundle-464a2af269.js', test: 'pan-zoom-js', module: true },

291 {match: 'div[data-pan-container]', src: '/static/js/pan-zoom-es5-bundle-2626f1bdf8.js', test: 'pan-zoom-js', nomodule: true },

292 {match: 'math,span.mathjax-tex', src: '/static/js/math-es6-bundle-d616f8e4f9.js', test: 'math-js', module: true},

293 {match: 'math,span.mathjax-tex', src: '/static/js/math-es5-bundle-66109c5184.js', test: 'math-js', nomodule: true}

294 ];

295

296

297 if (conditionalScripts) {

298 conditionalScripts.filter(function (script) {

299 return !!document.querySelector(script.match) && !((moduleSupport && script.nomodule) || (!moduleSupport && script.module));

300 }).forEach(function (script) {

301 loader.insert(loader.createScript(script));

302 });

303 }

304 }, false);

305 }

306 };

307 loader.init();

308 }

309 })(window, document);

310</script>

This suggested that the BM might be a metastasis ‘restrictive soil’ by encoding dormancy-inducing cues in DTCs. Here we show in a head and neck squamous cell carcinoma (HNSCC) model that strong and specific transforming growth factor-β2 (TGF-β2) signalling in the BM activates the MAPK p38α/β, inducing an (ERK/p38)low signalling ratio. Our work reveals a ‘seed and soil’ mechanism where TGF-β2 and TGF-β-RIII signalling through p38α/β regulates DTC dormancy and defines restrictive (BM) and permissive (lung) microenvironments for HNSCC metastasis. 356 <meta name="dc.description" content="In patients, non-proliferative disseminated tumour cells (DTCs) can persist in the bone marrow (BM) while other organs (such as lung) present growing metastasis. This suggested that the BM might be a metastasis &#8216;restrictive soil&#8217; by encoding dormancy-inducing cues in DTCs. Here we show in a head and neck squamous cell carcinoma (HNSCC) model that strong and specific transforming growth factor-&#946;2 (TGF-&#946;2) signalling in the BM activates the MAPK p38&#945;/&#946;, inducing an (ERK/p38)low signalling ratio. Importantly, systemic inhibition of TGF-&#946;-RI or p38&#945;/&#946; activities awakened dormant DTCs, fuelling multi-organ metastasis. Our work reveals a &#8216;seed and soil&#8217; mechanism where TGF-&#946;2 and TGF-&#946;-RIII signalling through p38&#945;/&#946; regulates DTC dormancy and defines restrictive (BM) and permissive (lung) microenvironments for HNSCC metastasis. Aguirre-Ghiso and colleagues report that the intensity of TGF-&#946;2 signalling dictates dormancy or metastatic growth of disseminated tumour cells by regulating the activity of p38&#945;/&#946; in different target organs."/>

737 <h1 class="c-article-title" data-test="article-title" data-article-title="">TGF-β2 dictates disseminated tumour cell fate in target organs through TGF-β-RIII and p38α/β signalling</h1>

793 <div class="c-article-body">

794 <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>In patients, non-proliferative disseminated tumour cells (DTCs) can persist in the bone marrow (BM) while other organs (such as lung) present growing metastasis. This suggested that the BM might be a metastasis ‘restrictive soil’ by encoding dormancy-inducing cues in DTCs. Here we show in a head and neck squamous cell carcinoma (HNSCC) model that strong and specific transforming growth factor-β2 (TGF-β2) signalling in the BM activates the MAPK p38α/β, inducing an (ERK/p38)<sup>low</sup> signalling ratio. This results in induction of <i>DEC2/SHARP1</i> and p27, downregulation of cyclin-dependent kinase 4 (CDK4) and dormancy of malignant DTCs. TGF-β2-induced dormancy required TGF-β receptor-I (TGF-β-RI), TGF-β-RIII and SMAD1/5 activation to induce p27. In lungs, a metastasis ‘permissive soil’ with low TGF-β2 levels, DTC dormancy was short-lived and followed by metastatic growth. Importantly, systemic inhibition of TGF-β-RI or p38α/β activities awakened dormant DTCs, fuelling multi-organ metastasis. Our work reveals a ‘seed and soil’ mechanism where TGF-β2 and TGF-β-RIII signalling through p38α/β regulates DTC dormancy and defines restrictive (BM) and permissive (lung) microenvironments for HNSCC metastasis.</p></div></div></section>

(<b>b</b>)&nbsp;Upper panel: representative live fluorescence microscopy image of a lymph node 4 weeks after surgery of the PT. Scale bar: 160 μm. Lower graph: number of disseminated HEp3-GFP cells in the lymph node of nude mice 4 weeks after PT surgery. n = 15 mice. (<b>c</b>)&nbsp;BM was collected from nude mice, and single cell suspensions were prepared as described in methods. Q-PCR for <i>Alu</i> sequences was performed on genomic DNA extracted from the indicated number of HEp3 cells serially diluted into individual mice BM cell suspensions. Q-PCR for <i>Alu</i> sequences was used to generate a standard curve from 10 to 10<sup>3</sup> HEp3 cells/BM by plotting the Alu <i>Ct-mGAPDHCt</i> against the number of cells per bone marrow (n = 3 BM samples per condition were assessed over 3 independent experiments) <b>(d)</b> <i>Alu</i> PCR was used to amplify <i>Alu</i> sequences in human (HEp3) DNA in BM cell suspensions from mice that carried HEp3 tumours and whose BM suspensions were apparently negative for HEp3-GFP cells when examined under the fluorescence microscope. The standard curve shown in <b>c</b> was used to calculate the number of HEp3 cells in these BM. (n = 3 (1, 4, 7, 9, 10), n = 2 (5, 6) Alu Ct values from independent qPCRs) see <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/ncb2861#Tab4">Supplementary Table&nbsp;S4</a> for the statistic source data. (<b>e</b>)&nbsp;Life fluorescence images from lungs at the time of surgery. (S = lung stroma). Scale bar: 160 μm. (<b>f</b>)&nbsp;Representative cleaved caspase-3 (C-C3) staining in PT-HEp3 (PT) (upper right panel), Lu-HEp3 (Lu, upper left panel) and BM-D1 (middle left panel) tumours. Scale bar: 40 μm. Representative P-H3 (right middle panel) and p27 (right bottom panel) staining in PT-HEp3 (PT) tumours. Scale bar: 40 μm. Arrows = positive cells. Lower left graph: Quantification of marker-positive cells. (n = 100 cells assessed/section. 15 sections assessed from 3 different tumour/condition). FOV = field of view. (<b>g</b>)&nbsp;Serial passage of BM-D1 cells on CAMs. Generation matched primary tumour (PT) HEp3 cells from the same animal were inoculated on CAM at (2×10<sup>5</sup> cells/animal) and transplanted weekly onto a new CAM (n = 5 (PT), 6 (BM) tumour nodules). (<b>h</b>)&nbsp;Dormant (BM-D1) and tumorigenic (BM-T1) BM-HEp3 cells were injected subcutaneous (s.c.) in nude mice (5×10<sup>5</sup> cells/animal). Graph: time, in days, it took for the tumours to reach 100mm<sup>3</sup>. n = 2 (BM-T1) 3 (BM-D1) mice, p = 0.0878 by unpaired t test. See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/ncb2861#Tab4">Supplementary Table&nbsp;S4</a> for the statistic source data. (<b>i</b>)&nbsp;Scheme adapted from (Kim, et al., 1998)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Kim, J., Yu, W., Kovalski, K. &amp; Ossowski, L. Requirement for specific proteases in cancer cell intravasation as revealed by a novel semiquantitative PCR-based assay. Cell 94, 353–362 (1998)." href="/articles/ncb2861#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d33379373e2817">25</a></sup>: 2.5*10<sup>5</sup> T-HEp3 GFP cells were inoculated on the chorioallantoic membrane (CAM) of d10 chicken embryos. 5 days after inoculation the embryos were sacrificed. The BM, liver and lung were isolated and inspected under the fluorescence microscope for GFP cells. (<b>j</b>)&nbsp;Number of disseminated HEp3-GFP-tagged cells (DTCs - HEp3-GFP) found in the chicken embryo lungs, liver and BM 5 days after inoculation. n = 10 (liver), 10 (lung), 7 (BM) Chicken embryos assessed. (<b>k</b>)&nbsp;Serial passage of BM-D2,-D3 and -D4 cells on CAMs for two weeks. n = 8 (BM-D2, w1), 6 (BM-D3, w1), 8 (BM-D4, w1), 7 (PT, w1), 4 (BM-D2, w2), 3 (BM-D3, w2), 3, (BM-D4, w2) tumour nodules assessed in 2 independent experiments. See <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/ncb2861#Tab4">Supplementary Table&nbsp;S4</a> for the statistic source data. Data in <b>c, d, f, g, h and k,</b> represent mean±s.e.m. In <b>a, f, g</b> and <b>k</b>, *p&lt;0.05, **p&lt;0.01 and ***p&lt;0.001 by Mann Whitney test. In <b>j</b> *p&lt;0.05, **p&lt;0.01 and ***p&lt;0.001 by One-way ANOVA-Bonferroni’s multiple comparison test.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig10"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-test="supp-info-link" data-track-label="supplementary figure 2 dec2 and p53 expression in " href="/articles/ncb2861/figures/10" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fncb2861/MediaObjects/41556_2013_Article_BFncb2861_Fig10_ESM.jpg">Supplementary Figure 2 DEC2 and p53 expression in HNSCC and breast cancer cell lines and in HNSCC patient samples.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>(a)</b> Lysates from 4T1, 4T07 and F3II cell lines were probed by immunoblot (IB) for the indicated antigens.
